[2:0:133,32] 9650   Health and Dental Benefits for Annuitants - Continued 

[3:0:66,69] The 2020-21 employer contribution for health premiums for employees hired by the state on and prior to December 31, 2016,  

[3:1:66,79] maintains the average 100/90 percent contribution formula established in Government Code Section 22871 for fully vested  

[3:2:66,89] members. Under this formula, the state averages the premiums of the four health benefit plans with the largest state enrollment  

[3:3:66,99] in order to calculate the maximum amount the state contributes towards retiree health benefits. The state also contributes 90  

[3:4:66,109] percent of this average towards the health benefit costs of each of the retiree's dependents. Vesting schedules and employer  

[3:5:66,120] contributions may vary by employee bargaining unit contract.  

[4:0:66,140] The 2020-21 employer contribution for health premiums for employees hired by the state on and after January 1, 2017,  

[4:1:66,150] maintains the average 80/80 percent contribution formula established in Government Code Section 22871.3 for fully vested  

[4:2:66,160] members. Under this formula, the state averages the premiums of the four health benefit plans with the largest state enrollment  

[4:3:66,171] in order to calculate the maximum amount the state contributes towards retiree health benefits. The state also contributes 80  

[4:4:66,181] percent of this average towards the health benefit costs of each of the retiree's dependents. Vesting schedules and employer  

[4:5:66,191] contributions may vary by employee bargaining unit contract.  

[5:0:66,211] The retiree is responsible for paying all health benefit plan costs that exceed the state contribution. Premiums are determined  

[5:1:66,222] on a calendar-year basis; therefore, the state contribution will vary during the fiscal year. The 2020 monthly contribution  

[5:2:66,232] maximums are $767 for a single enrollee, $1,461 for an enrollee and one dependent, and $1,868 for an enrollee and two or  

[5:3:66,242] more dependents. The 2021 monthly contribution maximums are $798 for a single enrollee, $1,519 for an enrollee and one  

[5:4:66,252] dependent, and $1,937 for an enrollee and two or more dependents. Dental care premiums vary by plan and number of  

[5:5:66,262] dependents.  

[6:0:66,283] Effective July 1, 2012, funding for health benefits for California State University annuitants is displayed in Organization Code  

[6:1:66,293] 6645 under Higher Education. This funding was previously budgeted within Organization Code 9650.

[7:0:204,279] 9658   Budget Stabilization Account  

[8:0:66,300] Proposition 2, approved by voters in November 2014, replaced the Proposition 58 (2004) version of the Budget Stabilization  

[8:1:66,310] Account (BSA) to build a stronger "rainy day" reserve while requiring accelerated debt pay down. Proposition 2 strengthened  

[8:2:66,321] the reserve by providing more stringent requirements to transfer funds back to the General Fund or suspend deposits to the  

[8:3:66,331] BSA, and increasing the reserve limit.  

[9:0:66,351] Proposition 2 requires a transfer from the General Fund to the BSA by October 1 of each year, as well as true up transfers  

[9:1:66,361] between the General Fund and the BSA for the two preceding fiscal years. In addition to the transfer to the BSA, a calculated  

[9:2:66,372] amount is appropriated for supplemental debt payments and other specified long-term liabilities.  

[10:0:66,398] LEGAL CITATIONS AND AUTHORITY  

[10:1:66,418] PROGRAM AUTHORITY  

[11:0:66,438] Section 20 and Section 22, Article XVI of the Constitution of the State of California.  

[11:1:66,448] Control Section 35.50, Budget Act.  

[11:2:66,466] Item 9658-011-0001, 2016 Budget Act and 2018 Budget Act.  

[12:0:66,503] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[13:0:66,522] 7760 - Proposition 2 requires the Legislature, through the 2029-30 fiscal year, to annually set aside in the BSA for a "rainy day"  

[13:1:66,533] 50 percent of the sum of 1.5 percent of estimated General Fund revenues and the amount of revenue from capital gains over 8  

[13:2:66,543] percent of General Fund tax proceeds that is not required to fund Proposition 98, and use the remaining 50 percent to pay  

[13:3:66,553] down debt. Beginning in 2030-31, 100 percent of the above sum would be deposited in the BSA for a "rainy day," reduced by  

[13:4:66,563] any amount up to 50 percent that the Legislature appropriates to pay down debt. The maximum balance in the BSA is limited to  

[13:5:66,573] 10 percent of General Fund proceeds of taxes for the fiscal year. Any amounts in excess of ten percent may only be used for  

[13:6:66,584] infrastructure needs.  

[14:0:66,604] Proposition 2 includes a true up mechanism for the two preceding years.  

[15:0:66,624] The Legislature may suspend or reduce the BSA transfer if the Governor declares a budget emergency. Withdrawal of funds  

[15:1:66,635] from the BSA is limited to half of the fund's balance unless funds in the BSA have been returned to the General Fund for  

[15:2:66,645] appropriation in the immediately preceding fiscal year.  

[16:0:66,665] Proposition 2 also establishes a Proposition 98 reserve whereby spikes in funding will be saved for future years. This will  

[16:1:66,675] smooth school spending and minimize future cuts. The Proposition 98 reserve does not change the Proposition 98 minimum  

[16:2:66,686] guarantee calculation.   See 9889 - Public School System Stabilization Account for more information on the Proposition 98  

[16:3:66,696] reserve.  

[17:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[6:0:66,227] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[6:1:66,246] 7765 - EQUITY CLAIMS  

[7:0:66,267] This program includes all claims approved by the three-member California Victim Compensation Board and the Government  

[7:1:66,277] Claims Program under the Department of General Services, and referred to the Legislature in the omnibus claims bills for  

[7:2:66,287] payment. The program provides an equitable procedure for the payment of the following categories of claims:  

[7:3:65,305] • Claims for which no appropriation has been made or for which no fund is available, but the settlement of which has been  

[7:4:76,315] provided for by statute or constitutional provision.  

[7:5:65,331] • Claims for which the appropriation made or fund designated is exhausted.  

[7:6:65,348] • Claims for which settlement is not otherwise provided for by statute or constitutional provision.  

[7:7:66,365] The Government Claims Program was transferred to the Department of General Services from the former California Victim  

[7:8:66,375] Compensation and Government Claims Board in July 2016. The California Victim Compensation and Government Claims  

[7:9:66,386] Board became the California Victim Compensation Board.  

[7:10:66,403] 7770 - SETTLEMENTS AND JUDGMENTS  

[8:0:66,424] This program includes claims paid through judgment and settlement bills sponsored by the Department of Justice each year.  

[8:1:66,434] The claims are either judgments against the state or settlements approved by the Department of Justice pursuant to the  

[8:2:66,444] authority provided in Government Code Section 948 et seq.

[8:0:164,474] 9800   Augmentation for Employee Compensation  

[9:0:66,496] This item reflects funding augmentations for state employee compensation. If the Legislature previously appropriated money,  

[9:1:66,506] through this budget item, to pay for the economic terms of employee compensation in previous fiscal years, the funding for  

[9:2:66,516] those economic terms is included in departments' budgets. When economic terms require funding not yet appropriated by the  

[9:3:66,526] Legislature, those funds are included in this budget item.  

[10:0:66,547] Additionally, this item sets aside funding for penalties the state may face under the Affordable Care Act (ACA). Beginning in  

[10:1:66,557] 2015, the state became subject to the Employer Shared Responsibility provision of the ACA. This provision requires large  

[10:2:66,567] employers to offer health benefits to full-time employees, defined as those who work on average 130 or more hours per month  

[10:3:66,577] (or 30 hours per week), and their dependent children. Under this provision, the state may be subject to penalties (Part B  

[11:0:66,587] Penalty), which may include part-time, temporary, and seasonal employees that may have been considered full-time for one or  

[11:1:66,598] more months, were not offered or did not qualify for health benefits through the state, purchased health coverage from the  

[11:2:66,608] Health Insurance Marketplace (known as Covered California), and received a premium tax credit or cost sharing reduction.  

[12:0:66,628] The ACA also contains reporting requirements, which require the state to track specified ACA-related employee information on  

[12:1:66,638] a monthly basis to identify the employees who meet health eligibility requirements, document whether benefits were offered,  

[12:2:66,649] and whether the employee accepted benefits. This data collection is used to report the state's level of ACA compliance to the  

[12:3:66,659] Internal Revenue Service on an annual basis. The state may be assessed penalties for inaccurate reporting (Internal Revenue  

[12:4:66,669] Code sections 6721 and 6722).  

[13:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[14:0:168,603] 9885   Reserve for Liquidation of Encumbrances  

[14:1:66,624] For individual department budgets, encumbrances (commitments for the procurement of goods or services which have not yet  

[14:2:66,634] been received by the state) are accrued as expenditures by departments at year-end and included in the expenditure totals.  

[14:3:66,645] This treatment is in accordance with the budgetary/legal basis of accounting and consistent with individual department budgets.  

[15:0:66,665] For the purpose of determining the overall General Fund balance, Government Code Section 13307 requires that  

[15:1:66,675] encumbrances should not be counted as a budgetary expenditure until the delivery of the goods and services. Furthermore,  

[15:2:66,685] Generally Accepted Accounting Principles (GAAP) require that encumbrances be reflected as a reserve against the General  

[15:3:66,696] Fund balance and not as an expenditure, as in budgetary/legal basis accounting. Government Code Section 13306 and state  

[15:4:66,706] policy require compliance with GAAP whenever it is in the best interest of the state. This budget reflects a statewide adjustment  

[16:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[3:0:66,69] to reduce expenditures on a budgetary/legal basis by the encumbrance amounts to comply with Government Code Section  

[3:1:66,79] 13307 and GAAP. A reserve of fund balance for encumbrances for this same amount is shown in Summary Schedule 1 for the  

[3:2:66,89] General Fund.  

[3:3:66,109] COMPUTATION OF ENCUMBRANCE ADJUSTMENT  

[4:0:66,130] The State Controller's Office accumulated a preliminary estimated General Fund encumbrance total of $3,175,060,000 from  

[4:1:66,140] 2019-20 year-end financial statements submitted by state departments. For budgeting purposes, encumbrances are estimated  

[4:2:66,150] to be at the same level for the 2020-21 and 2021-22 fiscal years and are assumed to be liquidated (paid) within the next fiscal  

[4:3:66,160] year. The Encumbrance Adjustment Table summarizes the methodology and the calculation for the encumbrance adjustment.

[1:0:162,66] 9889   Public School System Stabilization Account  

[1:1:66,87] Proposition 2, approved by voters in November 2014, established the Public School System Stabilization Account (PSSSA) as  

[1:2:66,97] a ”rainy day“ reserve for K-14 schools.  

[2:0:66,115] Proposition 2 requires Proposition 98 General Fund deposits into or withdrawals from the fund each year, as well as two  

[2:1:66,125] preceding fiscal years, when specific criteria are met.   Calculation of a deposit or withdrawal from the   PSSSA does not change  

[2:2:66,136] the Proposition 98 minimum guarantee calculation.

[5:0:122,130] 9900   Statewide General Administrative Expenditures (Pro Rata)  

[6:0:66,151] Central service agencies, such as Department of Finance, the State Treasurer, the State Controller, and Legislature, provide  

[7:0:66,162] budgeting, banking, accounting, auditing, payroll, and other services to all state departments. The Pro Rata process apportions  

[7:1:66,172] the costs of providing central administrative services to all state departments and funding sources that benefit from the  

[8:0:66,182] services. Amounts apportioned to special funds for their fair share of central administrative services costs are transferred from  

[8:1:66,192] the special funds to the General Fund and the Central Service Cost Recovery Fund.  

[9:0:66,213] Prior to 2016-17, Pro Rata charges to special funds were normally included in the appropriate departmental budgets. This  

[9:1:66,223] budget item included Pro Rata costs directly charged to special funds for those cases where appropriate funding was not  

[10:0:66,233] provided for in departmental budgets. Effective 2016-17, this budget item includes Pro Rata costs charged directly at the fund  

[10:1:66,243] level, rather than each individual appropriation, pursuant to Government Code section 11274.
